It orchestrates CPU allocation, memory management, device allocation, topology-aware resource placement, and dynamic resource allocation. The subsystem acts as a central hub that coordinates between the kubelet's pod synchronization loop and multiple resource-specific managers, enforcing kernel-level resource constraints through cgroup hierarchies.\n\n## Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe container manager serves three primary responsibilities:\n\n1. **Resource enforcement**: Allocates and enforces compute resources (CPU, memory, devices) to containers through cgroups and the container runtime\n2. **QoS hierarchy management**: Organizes pods into Quality of Service classes (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) with enforced resource isolation\n3. **Node allocatable enforcement**: Reserves resources for system daemons and kubelet components, ensuring pod workloads do not starve node infrastructure\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies (consumers):**\n- **kubelet.Kubelet**: The main kubelet sync loop invokes container manager for pod lifecycle operations\n- **lifecycle.PodAdmitHandlers**: Topology manager acts as an admission handler during pod scheduling\n\n**Downstream dependencies (providers):**\n- **cgroups (cgroup v1 and v2)**: Provides kernel-level resource enforcement via the cgroup filesystem\n- **container runtime (CRI)**: Kubernetes' abstract interface to containerized systems (docker, containerd, CRI-O)\n- **device plugins**: External plugins that provide specialized hardware resources\n- **DRA (Dynamic Resource Allocation) plugins**: gRPC-based drivers for claiming and preparing dynamic resources\n\n### Architecture Layer\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                    kubelet.Kubelet                          │\n│          (pod synchronization & reconciliation)             │\n└────────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────┘\n                         │\n         ┌───────────────┴────────────────────┐\n         │                                    │\n         ▼                                    ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────┐  ┌─────────────────────────────┐\n│  cm.ContainerManager        │  │  lifecycle.PodAdmitHandlers │\n│  (main interface)           │  │  (topology manager)         │\n└──────────────┬──────────────┘  └─────────────────────────────┘\n               │\n    ┌──────────┼──────────┬──────────┬──────────┐\n    │          │          │          │          │\n    ▼          ▼          ▼          ▼          ▼\n  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n  │  Resource Managers (inside container manager)  │\n  ├────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n  │ • CPUManager      (CPU pinning & sharing)     │\n  │ • MemoryManager   (NUMA-aware allocation)     │\n  │ • DeviceManager   (device plugin resources)   │\n  │ • TopologyManager (coordinate all above)      │\n  │ • DRAManager      (dynamic resource claims)   │\n  └────────┬───────────────────────────────────────┘\n           │\n    ┌──────┴──────┬──────────┬────────┐\n    │             │          │        │\n    ▼             ▼          ▼        ▼\n Cgroups    Device       DRA        Container\n(v1/v2)     Plugins    Plugins      Runtime\n           (gRPC)      (gRPC)        (CRI)\n```\n\n## Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 1. ContainerManager Interface (`container_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Central orchestrator and aggregator for all resource management functions\n\n**Key methods:**\n- `Start()`: Initializes all sub-managers with node topology and resources\n- `GetResources()`: Returns device and environment configuration for containers\n- `UpdateQOSCgroups()`: Periodically enforces QoS-level resource constraints\n- `GetCapacity()`: Reports node resource capacity to scheduler\n- `NewPodContainerManager()`: Factory for pod-level cgroup management\n\n**Files:**\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` (lines 66-170): Interface definition\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` (lines 100-140): Implementation struct\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go`: Windows-specific implementation\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_stub.go`: Stub implementation (unsupported platforms)\n\n### 2. Cgroup Management Subsystem\n\n**Responsibility**: Abstracts kernel cgroup interface (v1 and v2), converts Kubernetes resource concepts to cgroup parameters\n\n**Components:**\n\n| Component | Purpose | File |\n|-----------|---------|------|\n| `CgroupManager` interface | Cgroup creation, destruction, resource updates | `types.go:64-97` |\n| `cgroupManagerImpl` (Linux) | Dispatches to v1 or v2 based on kernel | `cgroup_manager_linux.go` |\n| `cgroupManagerV1` | Cgroup v1 specific operations (legacy) | `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` |\n| `cgroupManagerV2` | Cgroup v2 unified interface (preferred) | `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` |\n\n**Key behaviors:**\n- Manages `/sys/fs/cgroup` hierarchy\n- Converts internal `CgroupName` (e.g., `[\"kubepods\", \"burstable\", \"pod-id\"]`) to filesystem paths\n- Supports both `systemd` and raw `cgroupfs` drivers\n- Enforces memory, CPU, PIDs limits and QoS reservations\n\n**Example path conversions:**\n```\nInternal:    [\"kubepods\", \"burstable\", \"pod-123\"]\nsystemd:     /kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-pod-123.slice\ncgroupfs:    /kubepods/burstable/pod-123\n```\n\n### 3. QoS Container Manager (`qos_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Maintains three top-level cgroup containers for QoS isolation\n\n**QoS Classes and Cgroup Structure:**\n```\nkubepods (root node allocatable cgroup)\n├── guaranteed    (Pods with requests == limits)\n├── burstable     (Pods with requests < limits or partial requests)\n└── besteffort    (Pods with no resource requests/limits)\n```\n\n**Key behaviors:**\n- Creates and maintains QoS cgroup hierarchy at node startup\n- Periodically updates QoS container limits based on pod allocations\n- Reserves memory for burstable and best-effort via `--qos-reserved` flag\n- Implements `QOSContainerManager` interface\n\n**Configuration:**\n- Enabled via `--cgroups-per-qos` kubelet flag\n- Requires valid `--cgroup-root` path\n\n### 4. Pod Container Manager (`pod_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Creates and manages individual pod-level cgroups\n\n**Hierarchy:**\n```\nkubepods/burstable\n├── pod-uid-1   (enforces resource limits for this pod)\n│   ├── init-container-0\n│   └── container-0\n├── pod-uid-2\n│   └── container-0\n```\n\n**Key behaviors:**\n- `EnsureExists()`: Creates pod cgroup if QoS hierarchy enabled\n- Configures resource limits based on pod's QoS class and container requests\n- Disables CPU quota when pod has exclusive CPUs (feature-gated)\n- Enforces memory QoS via cgroup v2 `memory.min`/`memory.high`\n\n**Extensions:**\n- `podContainerManagerNoop`: Stub when cgroups-per-qos disabled\n- Memory QoS only available with cgroup v2 unified mode\n\n### 5. CPU Manager (`cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Allocates and pins CPU cores for containers, provides topology hints\n\n**Policies:**\n| Policy | Behavior | Use Case |\n|--------|----------|----------|\n| `none` | Shared CPU pool (default) | General workloads |\n| `static` | Pinned exclusive CPUs | Latency-sensitive apps, HPC |\n| `pod` | Pod-level pinning (static sub-policy) | Isolation between pods |\n\n**Key states and checkpointing:**\n- Maintains `cpu_manager_state` file in `--root-dir` for persistence across restarts\n- State includes allocated CPUs per pod/container\n- Reconciliation loop (default 5s) updates containers via CRI `UpdateContainerResources()`\n\n**Topology integration:**\n- Implements `topologymanager.HintProvider` for NUMA-aware allocation\n- Reports per-container affinity hints to topology manager\n- Respects topology manager's placement decisions\n\n**Resource coordination:**\n- Reads `--reserved-cpus` for system daemon reservation\n- Calculates allocatable CPUs: `all_cpus - reserved - system_reserved`\n- Exposes CPUs via `podresources.CPUsProvider` API for external tools\n\n### 6. Memory Manager (`memorymanager/memory_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Allocates NUMA nodes for guaranteed pods, enforces memory affinity\n\n**Policies:**\n| Policy | Behavior | Prerequisites |\n|--------|----------|---|\n| `none` | Shared memory (default) | Any system |\n| `static` | NUMA node pinning for guaranteed pods | NUMA topology required |\n\n**Key operations:**\n- `Allocate()`: Called at pod admission to reserve NUMA nodes\n- `AddContainer()`: Tracks container to allocated NUMA node mapping\n- Updates containers via CRI with cpuset affinity\n- Persists state to `memory_manager_state` file\n\n**Topology integration:**\n- Implements `topologymanager.HintProvider`\n- Provides per-pod and per-container NUMA topology hints\n- Works with topology manager's multi-source hint aggregation\n\n### 7. Device Manager (`devicemanager/manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Mediates between device plugins and containers, allocates device resources\n\n**Plugin model:**\n- Plugins register via Unix socket in `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`\n- Kubelet watches socket directory using plugin manager\n- Plugins implement gRPC API: `Allocate()`, `GetDevicePluginOptions()`, `GetPreferredAllocation()`\n\n**Resource allocation flow:**\n```\n1. Plugin registers with kubelet (GetDevicePluginOptions)\n2. Plugin announces available devices (ListAndWatch stream)\n3. Kubelet receives UpdatePluginResources admission request\n4. Container requests device resource at pod admission time\n5. DeviceManager.Allocate() calls plugin's Allocate() RPC\n6. DeviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions() returns device config\n7. Kubelet passes config to container runtime (mounts, envs, devices)\n```\n\n**Checkpointing:**\n- Stores allocated devices per pod/container\n- Survives kubelet restart; plugins must re-allocate matching IDs\n\n**Topology hints:**\n- Reports device NUMA affinity for topology-aware placement\n- Plugins can expose device topology via `TopologyInfo`\n\n### 8. DRA Manager (Dynamic Resource Allocation) (`dra/manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Manages lifecycle of resource claims for dynamic resources (GPUs, custom hardware)\n\n**Resource model:**\n- Pods reference `ResourceClaim` objects (Kubernetes API resources)\n- DRA drivers manage claim allocation via gRPC plugins\n- Plugins handle claim preparation/unpreparing on the node\n\n**Lifecycle:**\n```\nPod submission\n    ↓\nDRA Manager receives PrepareResources request\n    ↓\nFor each resource claim in pod:\n  1. Reserve claim on node (via plugin PrepareResources RPC)\n  2. Store prepared state in checkpoint\n    ↓\nPod starts → containers access prepared resources\n    ↓\nPod deletion\n    ↓\nDRA Manager receives UnprepareResources request\n    ↓\nUnprepare all claims (cleanup plugin state)\n```\n\n**State management:**\n- Caches claim info with version tracking\n- Reconciliation loop (default 60s) keeps in-memory state in sync\n- Survives kubelet restarts via `dra_manager_state` checkpoint\n\n**Coordination:**\n- Communicates with plugin manager to discover DRA drivers\n- Reports resource health status and updates via `Updates()` channel\n\n### 9. Topology Manager (`topologymanager/topology_manager_test.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Aggregates topology hints from all resource managers for NUMA-aware placement\n\n**Policies:**\n| Policy | Behavior |\n|--------|----------|\n| `none` | No topology enforcement; hints collected but ignored |\n| `best-effort` | Pods admitted if any NUMA node satisfies all hints |\n| `restricted` | Pods rejected if no single NUMA node satisfies all hints |\n| `single-numa-node` | Pods pinned to single NUMA node (restricted subset) |\n\n**Scope options:**\n- `pod`: Collect hints per pod (aggregated across all containers)\n- `container`: Collect hints per container independently\n\n**Hint aggregation:**\n- CPU manager → CPU affinity hints\n- Memory manager → NUMA node affinity hints\n- Device manager → Device NUMA affinity hints\n- All managers provide hints for the same NUMA node set\n- Topology manager selects NUMA nodes satisfying all hints simultaneously\n\n**Pod admission hook:**\n- Implements `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler`\n- Called as `UpdatePluginResources` handler before container creation\n- Validates topology feasibility; rejects pods if constraints unsatisfiable\n\n### 10. Internal Container Lifecycle (`internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Provides lifecycle hooks for resource managers during container operations\n\n**Hooks:**\n```go\ntype InternalContainerLifecycle interface {\n    PreCreateContainer()  // Before container creation (config setup)\n    PreStartContainer()   // Before container starts (add to manager tracking)\n    PostStopContainer()   // After container stops (cleanup tracking)\n}\n```\n\n**Invocation points:**\n- `PreCreateContainer`: CPU manager pre-allocates CPUs, returns in container config\n- `PreStartContainer`: All managers add container to internal tracking\n- `PostStopContainer`: Topology manager removes container (CPU/memory managers are called separately)\n\n**Usage:** Called by kubelet's `containerRuntime.RunContainer()` wrapper flow\n\n## End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### Flow 1: Node Startup and Initialization\n\n**Entry point:** `kubelet.NewMainKubelet()` → `cm.NewContainerManager()`\n\n**Sequence (from `container_manager_linux.go:207-391`):**\n\n```\n1. Validate system requirements\n   └─ Check cgroup v1/v2 mode, mounted subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset)\n\n2. Detect node hardware\n   └─ cadvisor.MachineInfo() → CPU count, NUMA topology, memory\n\n3. Initialize cgroup manager\n   └─ cgroupManager = NewCgroupManager(subsystems, cgroup_driver)\n   └─ cgroupManager.Version() returns 1 or 2\n\n4. Create QoS container manager\n   └─ NewQOSContainerManager() sets up Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort containers\n\n5. Initialize CPU manager\n   └─ NewManager(policy, CPUTopology, reserved_cpus, nodeConfig)\n   └─ Loads checkpoint state if exists\n\n6. Initialize memory manager\n   └─ NewManager(policy, NUMA topology, reserved_memory)\n   └─ Loads checkpoint state if exists\n\n7. Initialize device manager\n   └─ NewManagerImpl(topology, topologyManager)\n   └─ Starts plugin watcher in background\n\n8. Initialize DRA manager (if feature enabled)\n   └─ dra.NewManager() sets up plugin communication\n\n9. Initialize topology manager\n   └─ NewManager(hardware_topology, policy)\n   └─ Add all managers as hint providers\n\n10. Return cm (containerManagerImpl with all sub-managers initialized)\n```\n\n**File evidence:**\n- Lines 207-310: SubManager initialization\n- Lines 325-356: CPU/Memory manager creation and topology registration\n- Lines 358-389: Resource update channel fan-in setup\n\n### Flow 2: Kubelet Start (Container Manager.Start)\n\n**Entry point:** `kubelet.Run()` → `cm.Start()`\n\n**Sequence (from `container_manager_linux.go:615-710`):**\n\n```\n1. Build container map from runtime\n   └─ Query running containers, build (pod, container) → containerID mapping\n\n2. Start DRA manager\n   └─ draManager.Start(activePods, getNode, sourcesReady)\n   └─ Begins claim reconciliation loop\n\n3. Start CPU manager\n   └─ cpuManager.Start(activePods, sourcesReady, containerRuntime, containerMap)\n   └─ Loads checkpoint, reconciles with running containers\n   └─ Starts reconciliation goroutine (period from nodeConfig)\n\n4. Start memory manager\n   └─ memoryManager.Start(activePods, sourcesReady, containerRuntime, containerMap)\n   └─ Loads checkpoint, reconciles with running containers\n\n5. Get storage capacity\n   └─ If --local-storage-capacity-isolation: query ephemeral storage from cadvisor\n\n6. Validate node allocatable configuration\n   └─ Ensures kube-reserved + system-reserved < node capacity\n\n7. Setup node\n   └─ createNodeAllocatableCgroups() if --cgroups-per-qos enabled\n   └─ enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups() to set resource limits\n   └─ Create system containers (kubelet, runtime) if configured\n\n8. Run ensure-state goroutines (every 1 minute)\n   └─ SystemContainers execute ensureStateFunc callbacks\n\n9. Run periodic tasks (every 5 minutes)\n   └─ Update QoS cgroup limits, capacity reporting\n\n10. Start device manager\n    └─ deviceManager.Start(activePods, runtimeService, containerMap)\n    └─ Watches for new plugins, reconciles allocated devices\n\n11. Return success\n```\n\n**Resource update channel setup (lines 358-389):**\n- Creates single `cm.resourceUpdates` channel (buffer size 10)\n- Device manager and DRA manager emit updates asynchronously\n- Kubelet's main sync loop consumes updates to trigger pod re-evaluation\n\n**File evidence:** Lines 615-710\n\n### Flow 3: Pod Admission and Resource Allocation\n\n**Entry point:** kubelet's `syncPod()` → admission handlers → container creation\n\n**Sequence:**\n\n```\n1. Pod enters kubelet (via API server watch)\n   └─ Status: pod created in kubelet's working set\n\n2. Topology manager's PodAdmitHandler called\n   └─ topologyManager.Admit() (via GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler)\n   └─ Collects topology hints from all hint providers:\n      ├─ CPU manager.GetTopologyHints()\n      ├─ Memory manager.GetTopologyHints()\n      ├─ Device manager.GetTopologyHints()\n   └─ Applies topology policy (none/best-effort/restricted/single-numa-node)\n   └─ Returns admission decision + NUMA affinity if restricted policy\n\n3. Device manager pre-allocation (UpdatePluginResources)\n   └─ Called with pod admission attributes\n   └─ For each device request:\n      ├─ Check device availability\n      ├─ Call plugin.Allocate() RPC\n      ├─ Checkpoint allocation to disk\n      └─ Update NodeInfo.Allocatable\n\n4. CPU manager.Allocate()\n   └─ Called per container at pod admission\n   └─ Policy determines which CPUs to assign:\n      ├─ 'none': shares system CPU pool\n      ├─ 'static': exclusively allocates CPUs from reserved pool\n      └─ Respects topology hints if NUMA constraints exist\n   └─ Updates internal state (not yet applied to container)\n\n5. Memory manager.Allocate()\n   └─ Called per container at pod admission\n   └─ For 'static' policy:\n      ├─ Allocate NUMA nodes from free pool\n      ├─ Respect topology hints if NUMA constraints exist\n      └─ Update internal tracking\n\n6. DRA manager.PrepareDynamicResources()\n   └─ For each resource claim in pod:\n      ├─ Call plugin.PrepareResources() RPC\n      ├─ Get prepared resource information (CDI devices, etc.)\n      └─ Checkpoint prepared state\n\n7. Pod passes admission; kubelet proceeds to create pod cgroup\n   └─ NewPodContainerManager() returns pod-level cgroup manager\n   └─ podContainerManager.EnsureExists() creates pod cgroup:\n      ├─ Determines pod QoS class\n      ├─ Places pod under appropriate QoS container (guaranteed/burstable/besteffort)\n      ├─ Sets CPU quota if enforceCPULimits (unless exclusive CPUs)\n      ├─ Sets memory limits based on pod requests\n\n8. For each container in pod, kubelet calls InternalContainerLifecycle\n   └─ internalContainerLifecycleImpl.PreCreateContainer()\n      └─ (Placeholder; actual CPU config applied via UpdateContainerResources later)\n\n   └─ Container created by runtime (CRI CreateContainer)\n\n   └─ internalContainerLifecycleImpl.PreStartContainer()\n      ├─ CPU manager.AddContainer(containerID)\n         └─ Tracks (pod, container) → containerID mapping\n      ├─ Memory manager.AddContainer(containerID)\n         └─ Tracks (pod, container) → containerID mapping for cleanup\n      └─ Topology manager.AddContainer()\n\n9. Container starts (runtime.StartContainer)\n\n10. Reconciliation loops update containers\n    └─ Every CPUManagerReconcilePeriod (default 5s):\n       ├─ CPU manager:\n       │  └─ For each container with assigned CPUs:\n       │     ├─ Read container state from runtime\n       │     ├─ Call runtime.UpdateContainerResources(CpusetCpus=cpus)\n       │     └─ Update internal state\n       │\n       └─ Memory manager (similar reconciliation)\n```\n\n**Key files:**\n- `container_manager_linux.go:GetResources()` (lines 729-754): Device config assembly\n- `internal_container_lifecycle.go:PreStartContainer()` (lines 41-53): Manager registration\n- `lifecycle.go` package: Pod admission flow (outside cm subsystem)\n- `cpumanager/cpu_manager.go:Allocate()`: CPU allocation logic\n- `memorymanager/memory_manager.go:Allocate()`: Memory allocation logic\n\n### Flow 4: Container Resource Query (GetResources)\n\n**Entry point:** kubelet preparing to run container → `cm.GetResources()`\n\n**Sequence (from `container_manager_linux.go:729-754`):**\n\n```\n1. kubelet calls cm.GetResources(pod, container)\n\n2. DRA manager (if enabled)\n   └─ draManager.GetResources(pod, container)\n   └─ For each resource claim in container:\n      ├─ Lookup claim info in cache\n      ├─ Extract CDI devices\n      └─ Return CDI device list\n\n3. Device manager\n   └─ deviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions(pod, container)\n   └─ Returns DeviceRunContainerOptions containing:\n      ├─ Devices (block devices to mount)\n      ├─ Mounts (filesystem mounts)\n      ├─ Envs (environment variables)\n      └─ CDI devices (Container Device Interface references)\n\n4. Aggregate and return\n   └─ RunContainerOptions{\n        CDIDevices: [dra_devices... + device_devices...]\n        Devices: [...]\n        Mounts: [...]\n        Envs: [...]\n      }\n\n5. kubelet passes RunContainerOptions to runtime.RunContainer()\n   └─ Runtime unpacks CDI devices, mounts, env vars\n   └─ Container inherits device access, custom configurations\n```\n\n**Key insight:** All device allocation must happen before this call; GetResources only retrieves cached state.\n\n### Flow 5: Container Removal and Cleanup\n\n**Entry point:** kubelet terminating pod → `cm` cleanup calls\n\n**Sequence:**\n\n```\n1. Kubelet decides to delete container (pod eviction, termination, etc.)\n\n2. Runtime stops container (StopContainer, RemoveContainer)\n\n3. kubelet calls InternalContainerLifecycle.PostStopContainer()\n   └─ Topology manager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      └─ Clears container entry from affinity tracking\n   └─ Note: CPU/Memory managers clear state independently during pod removal\n\n4. Pod deletion from kubelet state\n\n5. Kubelet calls UnprepareDynamicResources(pod)\n   └─ draManager.UnprepareDynamicResources()\n   └─ For each resource claim:\n      ├─ Call plugin.UnprepareResources() RPC\n      └─ Remove checkpoint entry\n\n6. Pod cgroup destruction (podContainerManager.Destroy)\n   └─ Unmounts any cgroup controllers\n   └─ Removes pod cgroup\n\n7. CPU manager internally removes container\n   └─ On periodic reconciliation if not in active pods\n   └─ cpuManager.RemoveContainer() cleanup\n\n8. Memory manager internally removes container\n   └─ On periodic reconciliation if not in active pods\n   └─ memoryManager.RemoveContainer() cleanup\n\n9. Device manager cleans up allocated devices\n   └─ Marks devices as deallocated\n   └─ Checkpoint update removes pod entry\n```\n\n## Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Resource Allocation Failures\n\n**Scenario 1: No CPUs available (static policy)**\n- **Symptom**: CPU manager's `Allocate()` fails; pod admission rejected\n- **Root cause**: All reserved CPUs already allocated to guaranteed pods\n- **Mitigation**: Ensure `--reserved-cpus` or `--kube-reserved` not over-subscribed\n- **File evidence**: `cpumanager/policy_static.go` allocation logic\n\n**Scenario 2: Device allocation fails**\n- **Symptom**: Device plugin's `Allocate()` RPC fails or times out\n- **Root cause**: Plugin crash, insufficient healthy devices, plugin version mismatch\n- **Outcome**: Pod fails to admit; kubelet retries admission\n- **Mitigation**: Monitor device plugin health via healthz endpoints, implement plugin redundancy\n- **File evidence**: `devicemanager/manager.go:Allocate()` plugin RPC invocation\n\n**Scenario 3: Topology constraints unsatisfiable**\n- **Symptom**: Topology manager rejects pod under 'restricted' or 'single-numa-node' policy\n- **Root cause**: Pod's resource requirements span multiple NUMA nodes but policy forbids it\n- **Outcome**: Pod pending; will not schedule until resources become available\n- **Tradeoff**: Strict policies reduce latency variance but increase scheduling complexity\n\n### Cgroup System Limits\n\n**Cgroup v1 limitations (deprecated but still supported):**\n- Separate CPU controllers for CPU shares and CPU quota (inconsistency risk)\n- Per-subsystem hierarchies can diverge, complicating management\n- Memory controller lacks fine-grained control (no memory.min in v1)\n- **Mitigation**: Migrate to cgroup v2 (see `CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning` in `container_manager.go:52`)\n\n**Cgroup v2 requirements:**\n- Requires kernel ≥ 5.7 for full features\n- Root `cpu.stat` requires kernel ≥ 5.8 (see `CgroupV2KernelWarning` in `container_manager.go:54`)\n- Single unified hierarchy eliminates v1 inconsistencies\n\n### Memory Overcommit Risks\n\n**Scenario**: Pod memory requests < memory limits; kernel OOM killer activates\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Kubelet's eviction manager may not react fast enough\n- Kernel OOM killer selects victim processes (often unpredictable)\n- Pod may terminate abruptly without graceful shutdown\n\n**Tradeoff:**\n- Kubelet's `--eviction-hard` thresholds let kubelet proactively evict pods before OOM\n- Requires buffer between allocatable and pod requests\n- `--qos-reserved` reserves memory for burstable/besteffort pod protection\n\n**Design choice in `pod_container_manager_linux.go:92-96`:**\n```go\n// Pod cgroup memory.high set only if MemoryQoS enabled (cgroup v2)\n// Without this, burstable pod memory can eat into node reserved memory\n```\n\n### Device Plugin State Consistency\n\n**Challenge**: Plugin crashes mid-allocation; kubelet restarts\n\n**Design (from `devicemanager/manager.go`):**\n- Device allocations checkpointed to disk before returning to pod\n- On kubelet restart, checkpoint reloaded; plugin must return identical allocation for same inputs\n- Requires plugin idempotency\n\n**Assumption**: Plugin implementation guarantees allocation idempotency\n\n**Risk**: Non-idempotent plugin breaks across restarts\n\n### CPU Reconciliation Gaps\n\n**Scenario**: Kubelet crashes between CPU allocation and container UpdateContainerResources\n\n**Current behavior** (from `cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`):\n- State persisted to checkpoint before returning from `Allocate()`\n- On restart, reconciliation loop reads checkpoint and applies to running containers\n- Reconciliation period (default 5s, configurable via `--cpu-manager-reconcile-period`) is the update latency\n\n**Tradeoff**: Deferred application (reconciliation) vs. immediate application (more complex CRI calls)\n\n**Design choice**: Reconciliation simplifies failure recovery and reduces CRI chatter\n\n### Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) Claim Preparation\n\n**Scenario**: Plugin PrepareResources RPC fails; pod cannot run\n\n**Behavior** (from `dra/manager.go`):\n- Pod enters `PrepareDynamicResources()` phase\n- If plugin unavailable or claim preparation fails, pod stuck in preparing state\n- Kubelet logs error; pod stays pending\n\n**Recovery**: Depends on plugin availability restoration\n\n**Extension point**: Plugins can implement health monitoring via `dra-health` API\n\n### Syscall Constraints\n\n**Scenario**: `--protect-kernel-defaults` flag enabled\n\n**Effect** (from kubelet security settings):\n- Kubelet validates kernel tunable settings at startup\n- Enforces seccomp/AppArmor defaults\n- Any mismatch causes kubelet startup failure\n\n**Impact on container manager**: None directly, but affects node readiness\n\n## Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 1. CPU Manager Policies\n\n**Extension point**: Implement `cpumanager.Policy` interface\n\n**Methods to implement:**\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start(...) error\n    Allocate(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) error\n    AddContainer(...) error\n    RemoveContainer(...) error\n    GetTopologyHints(...) map[string][]TopologyHint\n    GenerateFirstInitialTopologyHints(...) map[string][]TopologyHint\n}\n```\n\n**Existing implementations:**\n- `policy_none.go`: Default shared CPU pool (no pinning)\n- `policy_static.go`: CPU core pinning for guaranteed pods\n\n**Usage**: Set `--cpu-manager-policy` kubelet flag\n\n**Risk**: Custom policies must guarantee idempotent state transitions; non-idempotent policies break across kubelet restarts\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go` (lines 47-72)\n\n### 2. Memory Manager Policies\n\n**Extension point**: Implement `memorymanager.Policy` interface\n\n**Existing implementations:**\n- `policy_none.go`: Shared memory pool (default)\n- `policy_static.go`: NUMA-pinned allocation for guaranteed pods\n- `policy_best_effort.go`: Dynamically prefer closer NUMA nodes\n\n**Usage**: Set `--memory-manager-policy` kubelet flag\n\n**Risk**: Memory pinning decisions impact pod latency; misconfiguration causes cache-miss penalties\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy.go`\n\n### 3. Topology Manager Policies\n\n**Extension point**: Implement `topologymanager.Policy` interface\n\n**Policy types** (from `topologymanager/policy.go`):\n- `PolicyNone`: Collect hints but don't enforce\n- `PolicyBestEffort`: Prefer single NUMA node; admit if any node satisfies all hints\n- `PolicyRestricted`: Enforce single NUMA node; reject pod if all nodes fail\n- `PolicySingleNumaNode`: Subset of restricted requiring exactly single NUMA node\n\n**Scope options**:\n- `pod`: Per-pod hint aggregation (hints collected across all containers)\n- `container`: Per-container hints (independent container placement allowed)\n\n**Usage**: Set `--topology-manager-policy` and `--topology-manager-scope` kubelet flags\n\n**Risk**: Over-strict policies (restricted, single-numa-node) reduce scheduling flexibility; under-strict policies (best-effort) may not achieve performance benefits\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy.go` and policy implementations\n\n### 4. Device Plugins\n\n**Extension point**: Implement device plugin gRPC API\n\n**Service definition** (from `devicemanager/plugin/v1beta1/`):\n```protobuf\nservice DevicePlugin {\n    rpc GetDevicePluginOptions(...) returns (DevicePluginOptions);\n    rpc ListAndWatch(...) returns (stream ListAndWatchResponse);\n    rpc Allocate(...) returns (AllocateResponse);\n    rpc PreStartContainer(...) returns (PreStartContainerResponse);\n    rpc GetPreferredAllocation(...) returns (PreferredAllocationResponse);\n}\n```\n\n**Key lifecycle:**\n1. Plugin listens on Unix socket in `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`\n2. Kubelet's plugin watcher discovers socket\n3. Plugin calls kubelet's `Register()` endpoint\n4. Kubelet calls `ListAndWatch()` stream (watch for device updates)\n5. On pod admission, kubelet calls `Allocate()` (per container per resource)\n6. On pod termination, devices deallocated (kubelet tracks)\n\n**Risk factors:**\n- Plugin crashes → devices appear lost until plugin restarts and re-announces\n- Plugin allocates non-idempotent resources → kubelet restart breaks consistency\n- Plugin returns stale topology information → topology manager makes suboptimal decisions\n- Plugin allocates more resources than declared → resource over-commit\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/plugin/v1beta1/` (API definitions)\n\n### 5. DRA Plugins (Dynamic Resource Allocation)\n\n**Extension point**: Implement DRA plugin gRPC API\n\n**Service definition** (from `dra/plugin/`):\n```protobuf\nservice DRAPlugin {\n    rpc PrepareResources(...) returns (PrepareResourcesResponse);\n    rpc UnprepareResources(...) returns (UnprepareResourcesResponse);\n    rpc GetResourceAvailability(...) returns (GetResourceAvailabilityResponse);\n    rpc GetClassParameters(...) returns (GetClassParametersResponse);\n}\n```\n\n**Key differences from device plugins:**\n- Resources are API objects (`ResourceClaim`), not kubelet-declared capacity\n- Plugins manage claim lifecycle (prepare/unprepare) across pod boundaries\n- Plugins provide health status feedback\n\n**Risk factors:**\n- Claim preparation timeout (no timeout enforced in current impl) → pod hangs preparing indefinitely\n- Plugin health deterioration → kubelet unaware until next claim prepare attempt\n- Claim state inconsistency after plugin restart → manual reconciliation required\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/` (manager and plugin interfaces)\n\n### 6. Cgroup Manager Drivers\n\n**Extension point**: Implement `CgroupManager` interface for alternative drivers\n\n**Current implementations:**\n- Linux systemd: Converts Kubernetes cgroup names to systemd unit names\n- Linux cgroupfs: Direct filesystem manipulation\n- Windows (separate implementation)\n- Unsupported platforms: Stub\n\n**Driver selection**: Auto-detected or set via `--cgroup-driver` kubelet flag\n\n**Risk**: Wrong driver for kernel configuration → resource limits silently ignored or cgroup operations fail\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` and versioned managers\n\n### 7. Pod Admission Handlers (Topology Manager)\n\n**Extension point**: Topology manager acts as `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler`\n\n**Call site**: kubelet's `syncPod()` → `podAdmitHandlers.Admit()`\n\n**Responsibility**: Validate pod's resource topology constraints before container creation\n\n**Hook returned by**: `cm.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns topology manager\n\n**Risk**: Topology manager bugs can orphan pods in pending state; policy misconfiguration causes entire workload rejection\n\n**File**: `topologymanager/topology_manager.go` (Admit method)\n\n### 8. Resource Capacity Reporting\n\n**Extension point**: `GetCapacity()` and `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()`\n\n**Usage**: Kubelet reports node capacity/allocatable to API server; scheduler uses for bin-packing\n\n**Risk**: Over-reporting capacity → scheduler over-commits; under-reporting → node under-utilized\n\n**Data source**:\n- Capacity from cadvisor machine info (physical hardware)\n- Allocatable = Capacity - system reserved - kube reserved - eviction thresholds\n\n**File**: `container_manager_linux.go:GetCapacity()` (lines 595-614)\n\n### 9. QoS Container Manager Customization\n\n**Extension point**: Override `QOSContainerManager` implementation\n\n**Default**: `qosContainerManagerImpl` (cgroups-per-qos enabled) or `qosContainerManagerNoop`\n\n**Customization hook**: `NewQOSContainerManager()` factory in `container_manager_linux.go:278-281`\n\n**Risk**: Custom QoS manager must maintain cgroup hierarchy; breaking hierarchy can cause resource leakage\n\n### 10. Plugin Registration Handlers\n\n**Extension point**: `GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` returns map of plugin handlers\n\n**Handler interface**: `pluginwatcher.Handler` (external to cm subsystem)\n\n**Registration flow**:\n1. Plugin manager watches `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/` socket directory\n2. On socket creation, calls handler for resource type (device, DRA, etc.)\n3. Handler manages plugin lifecycle (validation, monitoring)\n\n**Files**:\n- `container_manager_linux.go:GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` (lines 712-726)\n- Device manager and DRA manager implement handlers\n\n## Operational Implications: Performance, Reliability, and Maintainability\n\n### 1. CPU Pinning and Latency\n\n**Impact**: Static CPU policy (pinning) reduces latency variance for latency-critical workloads\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Guaranteed pods get exclusive CPU cores (no sharing with other pods)\n- Cores reserved via `--reserved-cpus` for system daemons\n- Reconciliation applies pinning every 5s (configurable)\n\n**Operational considerations:**\n- **Overallocation risk**: If too many guaranteed pods, run out of exclusive CPUs → admission failures\n- **Planning**: Size `--reserved-cpus` to account for kubelet, container runtime, system services\n- **Monitoring**: Track CPU allocation per pod; alert if utilization low (wasted cores)\n\n**Tuning parameters:**\n- `--cpu-manager-policy`: Change from 'none' to 'static' for pinning\n- `--cpu-manager-reconcile-period`: Lower value (faster reconciliation) increases CRI chatter\n- `--reserved-cpus`: Reserve more CPUs for system → fewer CPUs available to pods\n\n**File**: `cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` manager struct (lines 105-150)\n\n### 2. NUMA Topology Complexity\n\n**Impact**: Memory affinity and device locality decisions must account for NUMA topology\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Topology manager aggregates hints from all managers\n- Single NUMA node preference reduces memory latency (local access faster than remote)\n- Device locality affects throughput (GPUs, NICs attached to specific NUMA nodes)\n\n**Operational considerations:**\n- **Policy selection**:\n  - `none`: Safe default; simplest to understand and troubleshoot\n  - `best-effort`: Improves latency without hard guarantees; recommended for most clusters\n  - `restricted`: Strict resource co-location; only for latency-sensitive workloads\n  - `single-numa-node`: Most restrictive; rarely needed\n- **Asymmetric NUMA**: Some systems have unbalanced NUMA (different node sizes) → allocation algorithms may struggle\n- **Observability**: NUMA topology not directly visible to users; requires `numactl` or `/proc/cpuinfo` inspection\n\n**Monitoring**:\n- Track pod admissions by NUMA scope (single-node vs multi-node allocations)\n- Monitor memory latency if performance regression observed\n\n**File**: `topologymanager/topology_manager.go` (aggregation and policy enforcement)\n\n### 3. Device Plugin Reliability\n\n**Impact**: Device allocation failures block pod admission; device loss affects running pods\n\n**Failure scenarios:**\n- Plugin crashes → devices reported as unavailable; kubelet may deallocate and admit new pods\n- Plugin slow to respond → pod admission latency increases\n- Plugin state loss → devices appear reallocated incorrectly across restarts\n\n**Operational practices:**\n- **Plugin health monitoring**: Implement plugin-level health checks (heartbeat, resource validation)\n- **Redundancy**: Run plugin replicas with shared state (if plugin design permits)\n- **Graceful degradation**: Device plugin should report partial health if some devices healthy\n- **Resource reservation**: Reserve devices for system/monitoring pods; don't over-commit\n\n**Kubelet health checks**:\n- Kubelet monitors plugin socket availability\n- Unresponsive plugin may be evicted by plugin manager\n- Requires manual plugin restart\n\n**File**: `devicemanager/manager.go` plugin communication (lines 62-100)\n\n### 4. Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) Claim Lifecycle\n\n**Impact**: Claim preparation failures prevent pod startup; claim state must survive kubelet restart\n\n**Failure scenarios:**\n- Plugin unavailable during PrepareResources → pod stuck preparing indefinitely\n- Claim preparation succeeds but plugin crashes → claim state in limbo\n- Multiple kubelet instances claim same resource → conflict\n\n**Operational practices:**\n- **Claim ownership**: Resource claims should be namespaced to node; claims cannot be shared between nodes\n- **Plugin idempotency**: Plugins must accept re-preparation of same claim with same parameters\n- **Timeout enforcement**: Consider external watchdog if plugin hangs during preparation\n- **Health status**: Monitor claim health status field (set by plugin) to detect degradation\n\n**Checkpointing**:\n- Claim info and prepared state checkpointed in `dra_manager_state` file\n- Survive kubelet crashes; claims in \"prepared\" state on restart\n\n**File**: `dra/manager.go` claim preparation (lines 350-450)\n\n### 5. Cgroup Enforcement and Resource Limits\n\n**Impact**: Resource limits applied at kernel level; hard enforcement prevents workload expansion\n\n**Behavior**:\n- CPU quota (CFS) limits CPU time per period; kernel throttles exceeding processes\n- Memory limits trigger OOM killer if exceeded\n- Memory.min (cgroup v2) reserves memory; memory.high (soft) suggests limit\n\n**Operational considerations:**\n- **CPU throttling**: Containers hitting CPU quota experience latency spikes; monitor throttle counts\n- **Memory OOM**: OOM killer selection is unpredictable; prefer eviction-based pod removal via kubelet\n- **Swap**: `--fail-swap-on` prevents swap usage (recommended); without it, memory pressure causes swap thrashing\n- **Overcommit**: Pod memory requests < limits allows overcommit; requires careful monitoring\n\n**Tuning**:\n- Pod QoS: Guaranteed pods get priority in eviction; Best Effort pods evicted first\n- `--enforce-node-allocatable`: Enable to enforce node allocatable limits at node level (via kubepods cgroup)\n- `--memory-reservation`: Reserve memory for system via qos-reserved flag\n\n**Monitoring**:\n- Track CPU throttle events per container (via cgroup metrics)\n- Monitor memory pressure via PSI (Pressure Stall Information) metrics\n- Alert on OOM killer events in kernel logs\n\n**File**: `qos_container_manager_linux.go` (QoS enforcement, lines 84-140)\n\n### 6. Reconciliation Loop Gaps\n\n**Impact**: Delays in reconciliation loops mean resource constraints not immediately enforced\n\n**Behavior**:\n- CPU manager reconciles every `--cpu-manager-reconcile-period` (default 5s)\n- Memory manager similar reconciliation period\n- If pod created and immediately deletes container, reconciliation may miss cleanup\n\n**Operational considerations:**\n- **Latency sensitivity**: High-frequency pod churn (seconds) may not reconcile properly\n- **Reconciliation period tuning**: Lower period (e.g., 1s) increases kubelet load; higher period (e.g., 30s) delays enforcement\n- **Container runtime lag**: If runtime slow to return container state, reconciliation waits\n\n**Observability**:\n- Metrics: Track reconciliation loop duration, number of containers updated per loop\n- Logs: Reconciliation failures logged at INFO level\n\n**File**: `cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` reconciliation (lines 190-220)\n\n### 7. Node Initialization Latency\n\n**Impact**: Container manager initialization blocks kubelet startup; slow initialization delays node readiness\n\n**Initialization steps** (from `container_manager_linux.go:207-391`):\n1. Cgroup system validation (~100ms)\n2. Cadvisor machine info query (~500ms on slow systems)\n3. CPU/Memory manager checkpoint loading (100-500ms depending on pod count)\n4. Device plugin discovery (~1s if plugins slow to register)\n5. DRA manager initialization (if enabled)\n\n**Typical initialization**: 1-3 seconds for typical nodes; 5-10 seconds with many plugins\n\n**Optimization**:\n- Parallelize where possible (CPU/Memory managers can start concurrently)\n- Reduce checkpoint size (prune stale pods periodically)\n- Optimize device plugin registration (avoid RPC serialization overhead)\n\n**Operational**: Allow 10-15 second startup grace period before expecting pod scheduling\n\n**File**: `container_manager_linux.go:NewContainerManager()` (lines 207-391)\n\n### 8. Resource Leak Prevention\n\n**Risk**: Leaked cgroups, checkpoints, or device allocations persist after pod deletion\n\n**Leakage scenarios:**\n- **Cgroup orphans**: Pod deleted but cgroup not destroyed (disk full, permission errors)\n- **Checkpoint entries**: Stale pod entries in cpu_manager_state, memory_manager_state\n- **Device allocations**: Plugin crashes mid-deallocation; allocation persists\n\n**Prevention mechanisms:**\n- Periodic cleanup jobs: CPU manager prunes stale pod entries on reconciliation\n- Cgroup garbage collection: Stale cgroups cleaned up by kernel\n- DRA claim cleanup: ClaimInfo marked \"no longer needed\" after grace period\n\n**Operational**:\n- Monitor `/sys/fs/cgroup` for orphaned cgroups\n- Monitor checkpoint file sizes (should grow with active pods, shrink as pods delete)\n- Check device plugin allocation counts against running pods\n\n**File**: `cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` state pruning\n\n### 9. Multi-Kubelet Scenarios (Edge/Scaling)\n\n**Impact**: Multiple kubelets on different nodes may coordinate device plugins or claim resources\n\n**Constraints**:\n- Each kubelet instance is independent; no distributed state\n- Device plugins must handle multiple kubelet instances (e.g., two kubelets preparing same device)\n- DRA claims are node-local; scheduler ensures pod scheduled to claim's node\n\n**Operational**:\n- Device plugin architecture must be multi-kubelet aware (no shared state assumptions)\n- DRA drivers must handle per-node claim state\n- Ensure unique node names to avoid kubelet state collisions\n\n### 10. Upgrade and Rollback Considerations\n\n**Impact**: Checkpoint format changes during upgrades may require migration; downgrade may lose data\n\n**Checkpoint versioning**:\n- CPU manager checkpoint: Versioned format, supports migration\n- Memory manager checkpoint: Versioned format, supports migration\n- Device allocations: Ephemeral (not checkpointed across plugin restart)\n- DRA manager checkpoint: Versioned, persists claim prepare state\n\n**Upgrade path**:\n1. Stop kubelet\n2. Upgrade kubelet binary\n3. Kubelet startup loads old checkpoint, migrates if needed\n4. New kubelet writes checkpoint in new format\n5. Resume normal operation\n\n**Risks**:\n- Non-idempotent migration logic → data corruption\n- Downgrade after upgrade → checkpoint incompatible\n- Checkpoint loss → all allocations reset (CPU/memory re-allocated, DRA claims re-prepared)\n\n**Operational**:\n- Always backup checkpoint files before upgrade\n- Test upgrade path in staging environment\n- Allow extra time on first kubelet start after upgrade (migration runs)\n\n**File**: CPU manager state (lines 52-53): `cpuManagerStateFileName = \"cpu_manager_state\"`\n\n## Important Files and Directories\n\n### Core Container Manager\n\n| Path |
